# Install the Kaggle library
!pip install kaggle

files.upload()

# Create a Kaggle directory and move the kaggle.json file
!mkdir -p ~/.kaggle
!cp kaggle.json ~/.kaggle/
!chmod 600 ~/.kaggle/kaggle.json

# Verify Kaggle setup
!kaggle datasets list -s ravdess

# Download the RAVDESS dataset
!kaggle datasets download -d ejlok1/toronto-emotional-speech-set-tess

# Unzip the downloaded dataset
!unzip toronto-emotional-speech-set-tess.zip -d ./tess

print("Dataset downloaded and unzipped successfully.")

import os
import numpy as np

In [10]:
# Function to extract MFCCs from audio files
def extract_mfcc(file_path, max_pad_length=100):
    try:
        audio, sample_rate = librosa.load(file_path, res_type='kaiser_fast')
        mfcc = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=audio, sr=sample_rate, n_mfcc=40)
        # Pad or truncate MFCC to ensure consistent input size
        if mfcc.shape[1] < max_pad_length:
            pad_width = max_pad_length - mfcc.shape[1]
            mfcc = np.pad(mfcc, pad_width=((0, 0), (0, pad_width)), mode='constant')
        else:
            mfcc = mfcc[:, :max_pad_length]
        return mfcc
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error loading {file_path}: {e}")
        return None

# Path to the TESS dataset
DATASET_PATH = "./tess/TESS Toronto emotional speech set data/"

# Extract features and labels from dataset
def load_data(dataset_path, max_pad_length=100):
    features = []
    labels = []
    for root, dirs, files in os.walk(dataset_path):
        for file in files:
            if file.endswith('.wav'):
                label = root.split('/')[-1]  # Emotion is the folder name
                file_path = os.path.join(root, file)
                mfcc = extract_mfcc(file_path, max_pad_length)
                if mfcc is not None:
                    features.append(mfcc)
                    labels.append(label)
    return np.array(features), np.array(labels)

print("Loading data...")
X, y = load_data(DATASET_PATH)
print("Data loaded successfully!")

Loading data...
Data loaded successfully!

# Encode labels and one-hot encode
encoder = LabelEncoder()
y_encoded = encoder.fit_transform(y)
y_onehot = to_categorical(y_encoded)

# Reshape input data for CNN
X = X[..., np.newaxis]  # Add a channel dimension for CNN

# Split dataset into training and testing sets
X_train, X_test, y_train, y_test = train_test_split(X, y_onehot, test_size=0.2, random_state=42)

print(f"Training data shape: {X_train.shape}")
print(f"Testing data shape: {X_test.shape}")

Training data shape: (2240, 40, 100, 1)
Testing data shape: (560, 40, 100, 1)
In [19]:
def build_cnn_model(input_shape, num_classes):
    model = Sequential([
        Conv2D(32, kernel_size=(3, 3), activation='relu', input_shape=input_shape),
        BatchNormalization(),
        MaxPooling2D(pool_size=(2, 2)),
        Dropout(0.3),

        Conv2D(64, kernel_size=(3, 3), activation='relu'),
        BatchNormalization(),
        MaxPooling2D(pool_size=(2, 2)),
        Dropout(0.3),

        Flatten(),
        Dense(128, activation='relu'),
        Dropout(0.3),
        Dense(num_classes, activation='softmax')
    ])
    model.compile(optimizer='adam', loss='categorical_crossentropy', metrics=['accuracy'])
    return model

# Build the model
input_shape = (X_train.shape[1], X_train.shape[2], X_train.shape[3])  # Shape: (100, 40, 1)
num_classes = y_train.shape[1]  # Number of unique emotions
model = build_cnn_model(input_shape, num_classes)

print(model.summary())

plt.plot(history.history['val_accuracy'], label='Validation Accuracy')
plt.xlabel('Epochs')
plt.ylabel('Accuracy')
plt.legend()
plt.show()

# Evaluate the model on the test set
test_loss, test_accuracy = model.evaluate(X_test, y_test)
print(f"Test Accuracy: {test_accuracy:.2f}")

# Make predictions on the test set
predictions = model.predict(X_test)
predicted_labels = np.argmax(predictions, axis=1)
true_labels = np.argmax(y_test, axis=1)

# Decode the predicted labels
predicted_emotions = encoder.inverse_transform(predicted_labels)
true_emotions = encoder.inverse_transform(true_labels)

# Display a classification report
from sklearn.metrics import classification_report
print(classification_report(true_labels, predicted_labels, target_names=encoder.classes_))
